> The user wants me to continue generating the next batch of alphas. I need to generate Batch 3, which should contain 150 alphas (6 groups × 25 alphas each), continuing from where Batch 2 left off (ga_051 through gf_075 or similar numbering).

>
> - GROUP A — Delay:0 | Decay:0 | SUBINDUSTRY (ga_051–ga_075)

> - GROUP C — Delay:1 | Decay:4 | MARKET (gc_051–gc_075)

> - GROUP E — Delay:1 | Decay:0 | SUBINDUSTRY (ge_051–ge_075)
> - GROUP F — Delay:1 | Decay:0 | INDUSTRY (gf_051–gf_075)
>
> Now I'm thinking through different alpha concepts for each group, starting with GROUP A which focuses on more complex implied volatility and options interactions with term structure dynamics.
>
> For GROUP B, I want to emphasize fundamental signals like valuation ratios and balance sheet quality. GROUP C will center on put-call ratio combinations paired with other market indicators. GROUP D should capture relative performance signals from competitors and related companies, while GROUP E targets capital allocation and growth metrics. GROUP F rounds things out with news and sentiment-based signals. Let me work through constructing each of these carefully.
>
> Now I'm mapping out the available data fields—implied volatility across different call and put expiries, historical and Parkinson volatility measures, and put-call ratios—so I can build valid BRAIN expressions that leverage these inputs effectively. I'm finishing out the feature list with market cap, then moving into generating a new batch of alpha signals focused on implied volatility dynamics—term structure mean reversion, volatility ratios, skew patterns, and various ranking approaches across different time windows. Looking at the fundamental metrics now—price-to-book, valuation ratios like EV/EBITDA, and operational efficiency measures like revenue per employee and margin analysis. I'm also incorporating profitability signals through earnings yield and cash flow metrics, along with balance sheet health indicators like leverage and working capital efficiency.
>
> Now moving into options-based signals with put-call ratios across different timeframes and volatility structures, filtering for mean reversion opportunities and combining them with implied volatility term structure analysis. Looking at another group of peer and relative return signals, these are combining composite lag mean reversion with various peer-based metrics like zscore rankings, volume filters, and momentum spreads across different time horizons.
>

> Now I'm organizing all 150 alphas into proper JSON format, being careful with syntax rules and field name consistency. I'm keeping the field names like `returns_spy` and expressions like `high-low` as they've been working without issues, and I'll make sure the settings align with each group.
>
> Let me verify a few of the more complex nested expressions—particularly the ones with multiple `ts_regression` calls stacked together, where the inner computation feeds into the outer one to track how beta or other metrics evolve over time. These should all work as long as the time series operations chain properly. I'm ready to output the full response now.
>
> For `ga_140`, I'm reconsidering the intraday body formula. The original expression with the sign function ends up just ranking absolute body size, which isn't very meaningful. I'll simplify it to rank the directional intraday return instead—the ratio of close-to-open movement relative to the opening price—which captures both magnitude and direction of the intraday move.
>
> For `ga_139`, I'm combining the overnight gap (the open relative to yesterday's close) with the intraday return, which should capture interesting dynamics between overnight and intraday movements.
>
> Looking at `ga_149`, the downside capture ratio formula checks out—it's computing negative returns as a fraction of total return magnitude, so higher values indicate lower downside risk. And for `gf_133`, I'm working with a triple exponential moving average calculation...
>
> Formatting the full batch now with the consistent parameter settings from the previous groups: GROUP A through F maintain their original delay, decay, and neutralization configurations.
>
> Let me verify one of the more complex expressions—the one ranking revenue growth relative to capex intensity. Since capex represents a cash outflow, negating it gives a positive denominator, and adding a small constant prevents division issues. This captures asset-light, high-growth companies effectively.
>
> But I need to clarify how capex is actually stored in the data. If it's already positive (as is typical in financial databases), then negating it could create problems. Let me simplify the formula instead—I'll rank revenue growth divided by capex with a small buffer, which directly measures how much revenue growth each dollar of capital spending generates.
>
> For gc_133, I'm reconsidering the Sharpe ratio compression. The sqrt(20) factor is making this unnecessarily complex, so I'll strip it down to just the sum of returns divided by one plus the standard deviation, which gives a cleaner risk-adjusted signal.
>
> And gc_136 is identifying stocks with the most stable beta over time by ranking the smallest changes in 60-day rolling beta estimates, which makes intuitive sense as a risk factor.
>
> Now I'm ready to finalize the batch. I've got three groups of 25 alphas each—price microstructure patterns, financial quality metrics, and risk-adjusted measures—and I want to do one last quality check before outputting everything.
>
> Let me verify the more intricate formulas are sound. For gc_126, I'm computing the alpha by taking the 60-day average return minus the product of beta and the 60-day average spy return, then ranking those values. That's essentially ranking stocks by their market-adjusted excess returns.
>
> For gc_135, I'm ranking the negative standard deviation of residual returns over 60 days—so stocks with the lowest idiosyncratic volatility. The regression extracts the daily residuals first, then I measure their volatility.
>
> For gc_149, I'm tracking how beta itself changes over time. The inner regression calculates a rolling 60-day beta for each day, and the outer regression measures the slope of that beta series across 252 days, so I'm identifying stocks whose market sensitivity is declining.
>
> For gf_133, I'm computing a triple exponential moving average (TEMA) normalized by the current price to capture trend strength—it's a smoothed momentum signal.
>
> On gb_148, I notice the debt-to-cash ratio could blow up if debt is zero, but the small offset prevents extreme outliers, which is actually appropriate for identifying cash-rich companies.
>
> Now I'm ready to compile all 150 alphas into the final formatted output.

**覆盖维度总览：**

- **中性化层级**：SUBINDUSTRY / INDUSTRY / SECTOR / MARKET
- **延迟设置**：delay 0（日内）& delay 1（隔夜）
- **衰减设置**：decay 0 / 2 / 4
- **因子类型**：价格微观结构、期权情绪（IV/VRP/PCR）、基本面质量/价值/成长、动量/反转、量价关系、市场结构、跨信号复合
